### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 1 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company that makes wildlife videos purchases camera equipment for $\$ 32,400$. The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, after which it is considered to have no monetary value. How much is the camera equipment worth 4 years after it is purchased?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 10,800$
  B: $\$ 16,200$
  C: $\$ 21,600$
  D: $\$ 29,700$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  Therefore, the equipment depreciates at a rate of $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700$ per year.
  After 4 years, the equipment would have depreciated by $4 \times \$ 2,700 = \$ 10,800$.
  The current value of the equipment would be $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$.
  The answer is C: $\$ 21,600$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment has no monetary value.
  Therefore, the equipment depreciates at a rate of $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700$ per year.
  After 4 years, the equipment would have depreciated by $4 \times \$ 2,700 = \$ 10,800$.
  Therefore, the equipment is worth $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$ after 4 years.

  Therefore, the equipment depreciates at a rate of $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700$ per year.

  Therefore, the current value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 6:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, it has no monetary value.
  This means that the equipment depreciates $\frac{1}{12}$ of its value each year.
  After 4 years, the equipment's value will be $1 - 4 \cdot \frac{1}{12} = \frac{1}{3}$ of its original value.
  Therefore, the camera equipment is worth $\frac{1}{3} \cdot \$ 32,400 = \$ 10,800$ after 4 years.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 7:
Thought: 
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  This means that the equipment depreciates linearly over 12 years.
  Let's use the formula for the equation of a line to find the value of the equipment after 4 years.
  The initial value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400$.
  After 12 years, the value of the equipment is $\$ 0$.
  Using the two points $(0, 32400)$ and $(12, 0)$, we can find the equation of the line.
  The equation of the line is $y = -2700x + 32400$, where $x$ is the number of years after the equipment is purchased.
  To find the value of the equipment after 4 years, we plug in $x = 4$.
  $y = -2700(4) + 32400 = 21600$
  Therefore, the equipment is worth $\$ 21,600$ after 4 years.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 8:

  Therefore, the equipment depreciates $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12} = \$ 2,700$ per year.
  After 4 years, the equipment has depreciated $4 \times \$ 2,700 = \$ 10,800$.
  The current value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$.

  Therefore, the equipment depreciates at a rate of $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12}= \$ 2,700$ per year.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 2 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\frac{a-b}{a}=c$$In the equation above, if $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: $c>1$
  B: $c=1$
  C: $c=-1$
  D: $c<-1$
Response 0:
Thought:
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is negative.
  Since we are dividing a negative number by a negative number, the result is positive.
  Therefore, $c$ must be positive.
  We can't determine the exact value of $c$ based on the information given.
  Therefore, none of the answer choices are necessarily true.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is negative.
  Since $a$ is negative, $-a$ is positive.
  Therefore, $\frac{a-b}{a}=\frac{-1(a-b)}{-1a}=\frac{b-a}{-a}=\frac{a-b}{a}=-1\cdot \frac{b-a}{a}$.
  Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, $b-a$ is positive.
  Therefore, $\frac{a-b}{a}$ is negative.
  This means that $c$ must be negative.
  The only answer choice that is negative is D: $c<-1$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is negative.
  Since the numerator is negative and the denominator is negative, the result is positive.
  Therefore, $c$ must be positive.
  The answer is not A or D.
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is negative and $a$ is negative.
  Therefore, $c$ must be less than 1.
  The answer is not C.
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is negative and $a$ is negative.
  Therefore, $c$ cannot be equal to 1.
  The answer is not B.
  The only option left is A.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:

  Therefore, $\frac{a-b}{a}$ is negative.
  If $c$ is negative, then $\frac{a-b}{a}$ is positive.
  If $c$ is positive, then $\frac{a-b}{a}$ is negative.
  If $c=0$, then $\frac{a-b}{a}$ is undefined.
  Therefore, $c<0$ and the answer is D: $c<-1$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 4:
Thought: 
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is negative.
  Since we are dividing a negative number by a negative number, the result is positive.
  Therefore, $c$ must be positive.
  The answer is not A or D.
  If $c=1$, then $\frac{a-b}{a}=1$ which means $a-b=a$ and $b=0$. But we are given that $b$ is positive, so $c$ cannot be 1.
  If $c=-1$, then $\frac{a-b}{a}=-1$ which means $a-b=-a$ and $2a=b$. But we are given that $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, so $2a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, which is not possible.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $c=1$. 
Action: Answer("B")
Response 5:
Thought:
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is negative.
  Since $a$ is negative, then $|a|=-a$ and $|b|=b$.
  Then, $\frac{a-b}{a}=\frac{-a+b}{a}=\frac{b}{-a}=-\frac{b}{a}$.
  Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $-\frac{b}{a}$ is negative.
  Therefore, $c$ must be negative.
  The answer is D: $c<-1$.

Question: $$h(x)=2^{x}$$The function $h$ is defined above. What is $h(5)-h(3) ?$
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 4
  C: 24
  D: 28
Response 0:

  $h(5)-h(3)=32-8=24$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 24.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $f(x)=\frac{x^{2}-6 x+3}{x-1}$, what is $f(-1)$ ?
Choices:
  A: -5
  B: -2
  C: 2
  D: 5
Response 0:
Thought:
  To find $f(-1)$, we need to substitute $-1$ for $x$ in the expression for $f(x)$.
  $f(x)=\frac{x^{2}-6 x+3}{x-1}$
  $f(-1)=\frac{(-1)^{2}-6(-1)+3}{(-1)-1}$
  $f(-1)=\frac{1+6+3}{-2}$
  $f(-1)=-\frac{10}{2}=-5$
  Therefore, the answer is A: -5.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  To find $f(-1)$, we need to substitute $x=-1$ into the expression for $f(x)$.
  However, substituting $x=-1$ directly into the expression results in division by zero, which is undefined.
  We can use algebraic manipulation to simplify the expression and avoid division by zero.
  We can rewrite the expression for $f(x)$ as $f(x)=\frac{(x-3)(x-1)}{x-1}$.
  We can then cancel out the common factor of $x-1$ to get $f(x)=x-3$.
  Substituting $x=-1$ into this expression gives $f(-1)=-1-3=-4$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: -5.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 5 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A cylindrical can containing pieces of fruit is filled to the top with syrup before being sealed. The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, and the height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$. If $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ of syrup is needed to fill the can to the top, which of the following is closest to the total volume of the pieces of fruit in the can?
Choices:
  A: $7.5 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  B: $185 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The volume of the syrup is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The total volume of the can is the volume of the fruit pieces plus the volume of the syrup.
  The volume of a cylinder is given by the formula $V = \pi r^{2} h$, where $r$ is the radius of the base and $h$ is the height of the cylinder.
  We are given the area of the base of the can, which is $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$.
  The radius of the base is therefore $\sqrt{\frac{75}{\pi}} \approx 4.33 \mathrm{~cm}$.
  The volume of the can is therefore $\pi (4.33)^{2} (10) \approx 592.8 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The volume of the fruit pieces is the difference between the total volume of the can and the volume of the syrup.
  The volume of the fruit pieces is therefore $592.8 - 110 \approx 482.8 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The answer is closest to D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The can is a cylinder, so its volume is given by the formula $V_{\text{cylinder}} = \pi r^{2} h$, where $r$ is the radius of the base and $h$ is the height of the cylinder.
  We are given that the base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, so the radius of the base is $\sqrt{\frac{75}{\pi}} \approx 4.33 \mathrm{~cm}$.
  We are also given that the height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$.
  The volume of the syrup is given as $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The volume of the fruit in the can is the difference between the volume of the can and the volume of the syrup.
  Therefore, we need to calculate the volume of the can and subtract the volume of the syrup to get the volume of the fruit.
  $V_{\text{cylinder}} = \pi r^{2} h = \pi \cdot \left(\sqrt{\frac{75}{\pi}}\right)^{2} \cdot 10 \approx 235.62 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  Volume of the fruit $= V_{\text{cylinder}} - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} \approx 125.62 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The answer is not one of the given choices. The closest answer is D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.

Response 5:
Thought:
  The volume of a cylinder is given by the formula $V = \pi r^{2}h$, where $r$ is the radius of the base and $h$ is the height of the cylinder.
  The volume of the syrup is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$, which means that the total volume of the can is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  We can use this information to find the radius of the base of the can.
  We know that the area of the base is $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, so we can use the formula for the area of a circle, $A = \pi r^{2}$, to find the radius.
  Solving for $r$, we get $r = \sqrt{\frac{75}{\pi}} \approx 4.33 \mathrm{~cm}$.
  We can now use the formula for the volume of a cylinder to find the volume of the fruit in the can.
  The volume of the fruit is equal to the total volume of the can minus the volume of the syrup, which is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  Solving for the volume of the fruit, we get $V = \pi r^{2}h - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} \approx 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.

  Therefore, y=kx=4*5=20.

Choices:
  A: $(-5,-2)$
  B: $(3,-8)$
  C: $(4,-6)$
  D: $(9,-6)$

  We get $x=5$.

Context: $$.a=1,052+1.08 t.$$.The speed of a sound wave in air depends on the air temperature. The formula above shows the relationship between $a$, the speed of a sound wave, in feet per second, and $t$, the air temperature, in degrees Fahrenheit $\left({ }^{\circ} \mathrm{F}\right)$.
Question: Which of the following expresses the air temperature in terms of the speed of a sound wave?
Choices:
  A: $t=\frac{a-1,052}{1.08}$
  B: $t=\frac{a+1,052}{1.08}$
  C: $t=\frac{1,052-a}{1.08}$
  D: $t=\frac{1.08}{a+1,052}$

  Dividing both sides by $1.08$, we get $t=\frac{a-1,052}{1.08}$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $t=\frac{a-1,052}{1.08}$.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 10 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $2 w+4 t=14$ and $4 w+5 t=25$, what is the value of $2 w+3 t ?$
Choices:
  A: 6
  B: 10
  C: 13
  D: 17
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to find the value of $2w+3t$.
  We can try to eliminate one of the variables by multiplying the first equation by a constant and subtracting it from the second equation.
  Let's multiply the first equation by $-2$ so that we can eliminate $2w$.
  $-4w-8t=-28$
  $4w+5t=25$
  Adding the two equations, we get $-3t=-3$, which means $t=1$.
  Substituting $t=1$ in the first equation, we get $2w+4=14$, which means $2w=10$, and $w=5$.
  Therefore, $2w+3t=2(5)+3(1)=13$.
  The answer is C: 13.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
We are given two equations:
$2w + 4t = 14$  ...(1)
$4w + 5t = 25$  ...(2)

We need to find the value of $2w+3t$. We can solve this problem by eliminating one of the variables (either $w$ or $t$) from the two equations. Let's eliminate $w$ by multiplying equation (1) by $2$ and subtracting it from equation (2) multiplied by $-1$.

$-4w-8t=-28$
$4w+5t=25$
$-3t=-3$
$t=1$

Now that we know $t=1$, we can substitute it into either equation (1) or (2) to find $w$.

$2w+4(1)=14$
$2w=10$
$w=5$

Finally, we can substitute $w=5$ and $t=1$ into $2w+3t$ to get the answer.

$2w+3t=2(5)+3(1)=10+3=13$

Therefore, the answer is C: 13.
Action: Answer("C")

Question: If $x>3$, which of the following is equivalent to $\frac{1}{\frac{1}{x+2}+\frac{1}{x+3}}$ ?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{2 x+5}{x^{2}+5 x+6}$
  B: $\frac{x^{2}+5 x+6}{2 x+5}$
  C: $2 x+5$
  D: $x^{2}+5 x+6$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to simplify the expression $\frac{1}{\frac{1}{x+2}+\frac{1}{x+3}}$.
  We can simplify the denominator by taking the common denominator of $\frac{1}{x+2}$ and $\frac{1}{x+3}$, which is $(x+2)(x+3)$.
  Then, we can add the two fractions in the denominator and simplify the expression.
  After simplification, we can see which of the given choices is equivalent to the simplified expression.
  The answer should be the choice that is equivalent to the simplified expression.
Action: Answer("A")

  We can start by finding a common denominator for the two fractions in the denominator.
  The common denominator is $(x+2)(x+3)$.
  We can then combine the two fractions using the common denominator.
  The result is $\frac{(x+2)(x+3)}{2x+5}$.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $\frac{x^{2}+5 x+6}{2 x+5}$.

Question: $$(a x+3)\left(5 x^{2}-b x+4\right)=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$The equation above is true for all $x$, where $a$ and $b$ are constants. What is the value of $a b$ ?
Choices:
  A: 18
  B: 20
  C: 24
  D: 40
Response 0:

  We can start by expanding the left side of the equation.
  $$(a x+3)\left(5 x^{2}-b x+4\right)=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$
  $$5ax^3- abx^2 + 20x^2 + 12ax - 3bx - 12 = 20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  $$5ax^3- abx^2 + 20x^2 + 12ax - 3bx - 12 - 20 x^{3} + 9 x^{2} + 2 x - 12 = 0$$
  $$-15ax^3 + abx^2 + 29x^2 + 12ax - 3bx - 24 = 0$$
  We need to find the value of $ab$, so we need to isolate $abx^2$ term.
  We can do this by factoring out $x^2$ from the second term and the third term.
  $$-15ax^3 + x^2(ab + 29) + 12ax - 3bx - 24 = 0$$
  Since the equation is true for all $x$, the coefficients of each power of $x$ must be equal to 0.
  Therefore, we have the following system of equations:
  $$-15a = 0$$
  $$ab + 29 = 0$$
  Solving the system of equations, we get:
  $$a = 0$$
  $$b = -\frac{29}{a} = \text{undefined}$$
  Since $b$ is undefined, we cannot find the value of $ab$.
  Therefore, the answer is None of the Above.

  Therefore, the answer is not one of the available choices.

Question: If $a^{2}+b^{2}=z$ and $a b=y$, which of the following is equivalent to $4 z+8 y$ ?
Choices:
  A: $(a+2 b)^{2}$
  B: $(2 a+2 b)^{2}$
  C: $(4 a+4 b)^{2}$
  D: $(4 a+8 b)^{2}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can simplify the expression $4z+8y$ by substituting the given expressions for $z$ and $y$.
  $4z+8y = 4(a^2+b^2)+8(ab)$
  $= 4a^2+4b^2+8ab+4ab$
  $= 4(a^2+2ab+b^2)$
  $= 4(a+b)^2$
  The expression is equivalent to $(2a+2b)^2$.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $(2a+2b)^2$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
We are given that $a^{2}+b^{2}=z$ and $a b=y$.
We need to find an expression that is equivalent to $4 z+8 y$.
We can factor out 4 from $4 z+8 y$ to get $4(z+2y)$.
We can then substitute $z=a^{2}+b^{2}$ and $y=a b$.
We can simplify $z+2y$ to get $a^{2}+2 a b+b^{2}=(a+b)^{2}$.
Therefore, $4(z+2y)=4(a+b)^{2}$.
The expression that is equivalent to $4 z+8 y$ is $(2 a+2 b)^{2}$.
Therefore, the answer is B: $(2 a+2 b)^{2}$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:

  $a^{2}+b^{2}=z$
  $ab=y$

We can substitute $z$ and $y$ with the given equations to get $4(a^{2}+b^{2}+2ab)$.
We can simplify the expression inside the parentheses to get $4(a+b)^{2}$.
Therefore, the answer is (C) $(4 a+4 b)^{2}$.

  B: $f(x)=0.99 x+11.99$

  The slope of the line can be calculated as the change in shipping charge divided by the change in weight: $\frac{\$51.59-\$16.94}{40-5}=\frac{\$34.65}{35}=0.99$.
  The y-intercept is the shipping charge when the weight is 0, which is $\$16.94$.

  The answer is D: $f(x)=3.39 x+16.94$.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 18 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $a$ & $3 a$ & $5 a$ \\\hline$y$ & 0 & $-a$ & $-2 a$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of $x$ and their corresponding values of $y$ are shown in the table above, where $a$ is a constant. If there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, which of the following equations represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $x+2 y=a$
  B: $x+2 y=5 a$
  C: $2 x-y=-5 a$
  D: $2 x-y=7 a$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can use the given values of $x$ and $y$ to find the slope of the line.
  The slope of a line can be found by using two points on the line.
  We can use the first two rows of the table to find two points on the line.
  The first point is $(a,0)$ and the second point is $(3a,-a)$.
  The slope of the line passing through these two points is $\frac{-a-0}{3a-a}=-\frac{1}{2}$.
  The equation of a line with slope $m$ passing through a point $(x_1,y_1)$ is $y-y_1=m(x-x_1)$.
  We can use the point $(a,0)$ and the slope $-\frac{1}{2}$ to find the equation of the line.
  The equation is $y-0=-\frac{1}{2}(x-a)$.
  Simplifying this equation, we get $2y=-x+a$ or $x+2y=a$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $x+2y=a$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  To determine the relationship between $x$ and $y$, we need to find the slope and the y-intercept of the line that passes through the points $(a,0)$, $(3a,-a)$, and $(5a,-2a)$.
  The slope of the line is equal to the change in $y$ divided by the change in $x$.
  The change in $y$ between $(a,0)$ and $(3a,-a)$ is $-a-0=-a$.
  The change in $x$ between $(a,0)$ and $(3a,-a)$ is $3a-a=2a$.
  Therefore, the slope of the line between $(a,0)$ and $(3a,-a)$ is $\frac{-a}{2a}=-\frac{1}{2}$.
  Similarly, the slope of the line between $(3a,-a)$ and $(5a,-2a)$ is $\frac{-2a-(-a)}{5a-3a}=-\frac{1}{2}$.
  Therefore, the slope of the line passing through the three points is $-\frac{1}{2}$.

  We can rewrite this equation as $x+2y=5a$.
  Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ x+2y=5a}$.

Question: A circle in the $x y$-plane has center $(5,7)$ and radius 2. Which of the following is an equation of the circle?
Choices:
  A: $(x-5)^{2}+(y-7)^{2}=4$
  B: $(x+5)^{2}+(y+7)^{2}=4$
  C: $(x-5)^{2}+(y-7)^{2}=2$
  D: $(x+5)^{2}+(y+7)^{2}=2$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The standard equation of a circle with center $(h,k)$ and radius $r$ is $(x-h)^2 + (y-k)^2 = r^2$.
  The circle in the question has center $(5,7)$ and radius 2.
  Therefore, the equation of the circle is $(x-5)^2 + (y-7)^2 = 2^2$.
  Simplifying the equation gives $(x-5)^2 + (y-7)^2 = 4$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $(x-5)^2 + (y-7)^2 = 4$.

Question: On Saturday afternoon, Armand sent $m$ text messages each hour for 5 hours, and Tyrone sent $p$ text messages each hour for 4 hours. Which of the following represents the total number of messages sent by Armand and Tyrone on Saturday afternoon?
Choices:
  A: $9 m p$
  B: $20 m p$
  C: $5 m+4 p$
  D: $4 m+5 p$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Armand sent $m$ text messages each hour for 5 hours, so he sent $5m$ text messages.
  Tyrone sent $p$ text messages each hour for 4 hours, so he sent $4p$ text messages.
  The total number of messages sent by Armand and Tyrone is the sum of the messages they sent.
  Therefore, the total number of messages sent is $5m+4p$.
Action: Answer("C")

Question: A psychologist set up an experiment to study the tendency of a person to select the first item when presented with a series of items. In the experiment, 300 people were presented with a set of five pictures arranged in random order. Each person was asked to choose the most appealing picture. Of the first 150 participants, 36 chose the first picture in the set. Among the remaining 150 participants, $p$ people chose the first picture in the set. If more than $20 \%$ of all participants chose the first picture in the set, which of the following inequalities best describes the possible values of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: $p>0.20(300-36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  B: $p>0.20(300+36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  C: $p-36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
  D: $p+36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The total number of people who chose the first picture is $36+p$.
  The total number of participants is 300.
  The percentage of people who chose the first picture is $\frac{36+p}{300}$.
  The percentage of people who chose the first picture is greater than $20 \%$.
  Therefore, $\frac{36+p}{300} > 0.20$.
  Multiplying both sides by 300, we get $36+p > 60$.
  Solving for $p$, we get $p > 24$.
  Since $p$ is among the remaining 150 participants, we have $p \leq 150$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $p>0.20(300-36)$, where $p \leq 150$.
Action: Answer("A")

Topic: Math
Question: Which of the following is an equivalent form of $(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}-\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right) ?$
Choices:
  A: $-2.2 x^{2}+1.6$
  B: $-2.2 x^{2}+11.2$
  C: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$
  D: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+0.64$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's first expand the given expression.
  $(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}-\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right) = (1.5 x)^2 - 2*1.5 x*2.4 + (2.4)^2 - 5.2 x^2 + 6.4$
  $= 2.25 x^2 - 7.2 x + 5.76 - 5.2 x^2 + 6.4$
  $= -2.95 x^2 - 7.2 x + 12.16$
  Therefore, the equivalent form of $(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}-\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right)$ is $-2.95 x^2 - 7.2 x + 12.16$.
  The answer is C: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$.
Action: Answer("C")

Thought:

  $(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}-\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right) = (1.5x)^2 - 2(1.5x)(2.4) + (2.4)^2 - 5.2x^2 + 6.4$
  $= 2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76 - 5.2x^2 + 6.4$
  $= -2.95x^2 - 7.2x + 12.16$
  Therefore, the answer is C: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 26 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In the $x y$-plane, the line determined by the points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ passes through the origin. Which of the following could be the value of $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 4
  C: 8
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought:
  We know that the line passes through the origin, so the coordinates of both points must satisfy the equation of the line.
  The equation of the line can be found by calculating the slope of the line using the two points.
  If the line passes through the origin, then the y-intercept must be 0.
  Therefore, we need to find a value of k such that the line passing through the points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ has a slope that is equal to $\frac{k-0}{2-k} = \frac{32-0}{k-0}$.
  Solving for k, we get $k = 8$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 8.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The line passes through the origin, so we can find the equation of the line by using the slope-intercept form: $y = mx$.
  The slope of the line is $\frac{32-k}{k-2}$.
  If the line passes through the origin, then the $y$-intercept is 0.
  We can substitute the values of the points into the equation of the line to get two equations in terms of $k$.
  We can then solve for $k$ by setting the two equations equal to each other.
  The answer is the value of $k$ that satisfies the equation.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  If the line passes through the origin, then both points $(2,k)$ and $(k,32)$ must be on the line $y = mx$.
  The slope of the line is $m = \frac{32-k}{k-2}$.
  If the line passes through the origin, then $k=2m$.
  Substituting $k=2m$ into the equation of the slope, we get $m=\frac{32-2m}{2m-2}$.
  Solving for $m$, we get $m=\frac{16}{m-1}$.
  Therefore, $m^2-16m+16=0$.
  The solutions to this quadratic are $m=8\pm4\sqrt{3}$.
  If $m=8+4\sqrt{3}$, then $k=2m=16+8\sqrt{3}$, which is not in the answer choices.
  If $m=8-4\sqrt{3}$, then $k=2m=16-8\sqrt{3}$, which is not in the answer choices.
  Therefore, the answer is None of the Above.

  If the line passes through the origin, then the two points must be on the opposite sides of the origin.

  B: 100
  C: 200

To solve the problem, we need to find the percent increase from 2012 to 2013 and the percent increase from 2013 to 2014. We can then use this information to find the expected number of subscriptions sold in 2014.

From 2012 to 2013, the number of subscriptions sold increased by:
(5,880 - 5,600) / 5,600 = 0.05 or 5%

Let x be the percent increase from 2013 to 2014. Then, the percent increase from 2012 to 2014 is 2x.

From 2013 to 2014, the number of subscriptions sold would increase by:
5,880 * x / 100

From 2012 to 2014, the number of subscriptions sold would increase by:
5,600 * (2x) / 100 = 112x / 100

We know that the percent increase from 2012 to 2013 is 5%. Therefore, we can set up the following equation:

5,880 * x / 100 = 5,880 * 0.05 + 5,600 + 112x / 100

Solving for x, we get:

x = 4.5%

To find the expected number of subscriptions sold in 2014, we can use:

5,880 * 4.5 / 100 = 264.6

Rounding to the nearest whole number, we get:

265 + 5,880 = 6,145

Therefore, the manager expected 6,145 subscriptions to be sold in 2014.

Question: A customer paid $\$ 53.00$ for a jacket after a 6 percent sales tax was added. What was the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 47.60$
  B: $\$ 50.00$
  C: $\$ 52.60$
  D: $\$ 52.84$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added is $x$.
  The sales tax is 6% of the price of the jacket before tax, which is $0.06x$.
  The total cost of the jacket is the sum of the price before tax and the sales tax, which is $x + 0.06x = 1.06x$.
  We know that the total cost of the jacket is $\$ 53.00$.
  Therefore, we can set up the equation $1.06x = 53$ and solve for $x$.
  $1.06x = 53$
  $x = \frac{53}{1.06}$
  $x \approx 50$
  Therefore, the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added was $\$ 50.00$.

  B: $P(t)=4(1.9)^{t}$
  C: $P(t)=1.19 t+4$
  D: $P(t)=1.019 t+4$

Question: If a white birch tree and a pin oak tree each now have a diameter of 1 foot, which of the following will be closest to the difference, in inches, of their diameters 10 years from now? $(1$ foot $=12$ inches $)$
Choices:
  A: 1.0
  B: 1.2
  C: 1.3
  D: 1.4
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the diameter of the white birch tree and the pin oak tree will increase by the same percentage each year.
  We can use the formula $d = r \cdot t$, where $d$ is the diameter, $r$ is the rate of growth, and $t$ is the time in years.
  Let's assume that the rate of growth is $r$ percent per year.
  After 10 years, the diameter of each tree will be $d = (1 + r)^{10}$ feet.
  The difference in their diameters will be $(1 + r)^{10} - (1 + r)^{10} = (1 + r)^{10} - (1 + r)^{10} = 0$ feet.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 1.0.

Question: $$\left(x^{2} y-3 y^{2}+5 x y^{2}\right)-\left(-x^{2} y+3 x y^{2}-3 y^{2}\right)$$Which of the following is equivalent to the expression above?
Choices:
  A: $4 x^{2} y^{2}$
  B: $8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$
  C: $2 x^{2} y+2 x y^{2}$
  D: $2 x^{2} y+8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$

  $$=x^{2} y-3 y^{2}+5 x y^{2}+x^{2} y-3 x y^{2}+3 y^{2}$$
  $$=2 x^{2} y+2 x y^{2}$$
  Therefore, the answer is C: $2 x^{2} y+2 x y^{2}$.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 36 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company purchased a machine valued at $\$ 120,000$. The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year so that after 10 years the value will be $\$ 30,000$. Which of the following equations gives the value, $v$, of the machine, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased for $0 \leq t \leq 10 ?$
Choices:
  A: $v=30,000-9,000 t$
  B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$
  C: $v=120,000+9,000 t$
  D: $v=120,000-30,000 t$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The machine depreciates by the same amount each year.
  The initial value of the machine is $\$120,000$.
  After 10 years, the value of the machine is $\$30,000$.
  We can find the amount of depreciation per year by dividing the difference in value by the number of years.
  The amount of depreciation per year is $(120,000-30,000)/10 = 9,000$.
  The value of the machine, $v$, after $t$ years can be found by subtracting the amount of depreciation from the initial value.
  Therefore, the equation that gives the value of the machine, $v$, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased is $v=120,000-9,000 t$.
  The answer is B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year.
  After 10 years, the value of the machine will be $\$30,000$.
  The initial value of the machine is $\$120,000$.
  The value of the machine decreases linearly over time.
  Therefore, we can use the slope-intercept form of a linear equation to model the value of the machine over time.
  The slope of the line is the amount by which the value of the machine decreases each year.
  The initial value of the machine is the y-intercept of the line.
  The equation of the line is $v = mt + b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  We can use the given information to find the slope and y-intercept of the line.
  The slope is $\frac{120,000-30,000}{10-0}=-9,000$.
  The y-intercept is $120,000$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $v=-9,000t+120,000$.
  The answer is B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$.
Action: Answer("B")

  The slope of the line is the depreciation per year, which is $(120,000 - 30,000)/10 = 9,000$.
  The initial value of the machine corresponds to the point $(0, 120,000)$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $v = -9,000t + 120,000$.
  We are asked to find the value of the machine for $0 \leq t \leq 10$, which means we need to check if $v = 30,000$ when $t = 10$.
  Plugging in $t = 10$ gives $v = -9,000(10) + 120,000 = 30,000$, which is consistent with the given information.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$.

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& x=y-3 \\& \frac{x}{2}+2 y=6\end{aligned}$$Which ordered pair $(x, y)$ satisfies the system of equations shown above?
Choices:
  A: $(-3,0)$
  B: $(0,3)$
  C: $(6,-3)$
  D: $(36,-6)$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We have two equations and two unknowns.
  We can solve for one variable in terms of the other in the first equation.
  We can substitute this expression into the second equation to get an equation in one variable.
  We can solve this equation to find the value of the variable.
  We can substitute this value back into the first equation to find the value of the other variable.
  We can check which ordered pair satisfies both equations.
  
Action: 
  Solving for x in terms of y in the first equation, we get $x=y-3$.
  Substituting this expression into the second equation, we get $\frac{y-3}{2}+2y=6$.
  Simplifying this equation, we get $5y=15$, so $y=3$.
  Substituting this value back into the first equation, we get $x=0$.
  Therefore, the ordered pair $(x,y)$ that satisfies the system of equations is $(0,3)$.
  The answer is B: $(0,3)$.

  We get $y=3$.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 38 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Ken is working this summer as part of a crew on a farm. He earned $\$ 8$ per hour for the first 10 hours he worked this week. Because of his performance, his crew leader raised his salary to $\$ 10$ per hour for the rest of the week. Ken saves $90 \%$ of his earnings from each week. What is the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week?
Choices:
  A: 38
  B: 33
  C: 22
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought:
  Ken earned $\$ 8$ per hour for the first 10 hours he worked, so he earned $\$ 8 \cdot 10 = \$ 80$ for the first 10 hours.
  Let $h$ be the number of hours Ken works for the rest of the week.
  Ken earned $\$ 10$ per hour for the rest of the week, so he earned $\$ 10h$ for the rest of the week.
  Ken saves $90 \%$ of his earnings from each week, so he saves $0.9(\$ 80 + \$ 10h) = \$ 72 + \$ 9h$ for the week.
  We want to find the least number of hours $h$ he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week.
  We can set up an inequality: $\$ 72 + \$ 9h \geq \$ 270$.
  Solving for $h$, we get $h \geq \frac{198}{9} \approx 22$.
  The least integer greater than or equal to $\frac{198}{9}$ is 22.
  Therefore, Ken must work at least 22 hours for the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week.
  The answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C) }22}$. 
Action: Answer("C")

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 39 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A cargo helicopter delivers only 100-pound packages and 120-pound packages. For each delivery trip, the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages, and the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds. What is the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 4
  C: 5
  D: 6
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's assume that the helicopter carries x 100-pound packages and y 120-pound packages.
From the problem, we know that:
- x + y >= 10 (the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages)
- 100x + 120y <= 1100 (the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds)

We want to find the maximum value of y, the number of 120-pound packages.

We can simplify the second inequality by dividing both sides by 20:
- 5x + 6y <= 55

We can then solve for x in terms of y:
- x >= 10 - y

Substituting this into the second inequality:
- 5(10-y) + 6y <= 55
- 50 - 5y + 6y <= 55
- y <= 5

Therefore, the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip is 5.

  B: Kathy starts each week with 108 phones to fix.
  C: Kathy repairs phones at a rate of 108 per hour.
  D: Kathy repairs phones at a rate of 108 per day.

  The variable $d$ represents the number of days that Kathy has worked.

  The answer is B: Kathy starts each week with 108 phones to fix.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 41 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In the $x y$-plane, the graph of which of the following equations is a line with a slope of 3 ?
Choices:
  A: $y=\frac{1}{3} x$
  B: $y=x-3$
  C: $y=3 x+2$
  D: $y=6 x+3$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The slope-intercept form of a linear equation is $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  If a line has a slope of 3, then its equation can be written as $y=3x+b$ for some value of $b$.
  Therefore, we need to find the equation that can be written in this form.
  The answer is C: $y=3x+2$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The slope-intercept form of a linear equation is $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  The equation is a line with a slope of 3, so we are looking for an equation in slope-intercept form with $m=3$.
  Therefore, the answer is either C or D.
  To confirm, we can check that the slope of the line given by each equation is indeed 3.
  The slope of the line given by C is 3, so C is the answer.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  The slope of a line is the ratio of the change in the y-coordinates to the change in the x-coordinates between any two points on the line.
  Therefore, we can rewrite each equation in slope-intercept form, $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope of the line.
  A: $y=\frac{1}{3} x$ can be rewritten as $y=\frac{1}{3} x+0$, so the slope is $\frac{1}{3}$.

Question: Which of the following complex numbers is equal to $(5+12 i)-\left(9 i^{2}-6 i\right)$, for $i=\sqrt{-1}$ ?

  A: $-14-18 i$
  B: $-4-6 i$
  C: $4+6 i$
  D: $14+18 i$
Response 0:
Thought:
  $i^{2}=-1$
  $\left(9 i^{2}-6 i\right)=\left(9(-1)-6 i\right)=(-9-6i)$
  $(5+12i)-(-9-6i)=14+18i$
  Therefore, the answer is D: $14+18i$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:

Therefore, $(5+12 i)-\left(9 i^{2}-6 i\right) = (5+12i) - (-9-6i) = 14+18i$.
So, the answer is D: $14+18i$.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 45 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In the $x y$-plane, the parabola with equation $y=(x-11)^{2}$ intersects the line with equation $y=25$ at two points, $A$ and $B$. What is the length of $\overline{A B}$ ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 12
  C: 14
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to find the $x$-coordinates of the points of intersection of the parabola and the line $y=25$.
  Setting $y$ equal to $25$ in the equation of the parabola, we get $25=(x-11)^2$.
  Taking the square root of both sides, we get $x-11=\pm5$, which gives us $x=6$ and $x=16$.
  Therefore, the distance between the points $A$ and $B$ is $|6-16|=10$.
  The answer is A: 10.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The equation of the parabola is $y=(x-11)^2$.
  The equation of the line is $y=25$.
  To find the intersection points, we set the two equations equal to each other and solve for $x$.
  $(x-11)^2 = 25$
  Taking the square root of both sides, we get $x-11 = \pm 5$.
  Solving for $x$, we get $x=6$ or $x=16$.
  Therefore, the intersection points are $(6,25)$ and $(16,25)$.
  The length of $\overline{AB}$ is the difference between the $x$-coordinates of the two points.
  $AB = 16-6 = 10$.
  The answer is A: 10.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
  To find the length of $\overline{A B}$, we need to find the $x$-coordinates of points $A$ and $B$.
  Since the parabola intersects the line $y=25$ at two points, we can set $(x-11)^2 = 25$ and solve for $x$.
  $(x-11)^2 = 25$ can be rewritten as $(x-11)(x-11) = 25$.
  By using the zero product property, we can get two possible values of $x$: $x-11=5$ and $x-11=-5$.
  Solving for $x$ gives us $x=16$ and $x=6$.
  Therefore, the $x$-coordinates of points $A$ and $B$ are $16$ and $6$, respectively.
  The length of $\overline{A B}$ is the absolute difference between $16$ and $6$, which is $10$.
  The answer is A: 10.

  $y_{B}=(16-11)^{2}=25$
  So, the $y$ coordinates of points $A$ and $B$ are both $25$.

  The equation of the parabola is $y=(x-11)^2$.
  The equation of the line is $y=25$.
  To find the intersection points, we need to solve the system of equations $y=(x-11)^2$ and $y=25$.
  Setting the two equations equal to each other, we get $(x-11)^2=25$.
  Taking the square root of both sides, we get $x-11=\pm 5$.
  Solving for $x$, we get $x=6$ or $x=16$.

  Therefore, the two intersection points are $(6,25)$ and $(16,25)$.

  The equation of the line is $y=25$.
  To find the intersection points, we need to solve the system of equations: 
  $(x-11)^2=25$ and $y=25$.
  Solving the first equation, we get $x-11=\pm5$, which gives us $x=6$ or $x=16$.
  Therefore, the intersection points are $(6,25)$ and $(16,25)$.
  The length of $\overline{AB}$ is the distance between these two points.
  Using the distance formula, we get $\sqrt{(16-6)^2+(25-25)^2}=\sqrt{100}=10$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 10.

Question: Oil and gas production in a certain area dropped from 4 million barrels in 2000 to 1.9 million barrels in 2013. Assuming that the oil and gas production decreased at a constant rate, which of the following linear functions $f$ best models the production, in millions of barrels, $t$ years after the year 2000 ?
Choices:
  A: $f(t)=\frac{21}{130} t+4$
  B: $f(t)=\frac{19}{130} t+4$
  C: $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130} t+4$
  D: $f(t)=-\frac{19}{130} t+4$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The oil and gas production dropped from 4 million barrels in 2000 to 1.9 million barrels in 2013.
  The difference between the production in 2000 and 2013 is 4 - 1.9 = 2.1 million barrels.
  The production decreased over 13 years (from 2000 to 2013).
  Therefore, the production decreased at a constant rate of 2.1/13 million barrels per year.
  Let $f(t)$ be the production, in millions of barrels, $t$ years after the year 2000.
  We know that $f(0) = 4$ and $f(13) = 1.9$.
  We can use the point-slope form of a linear function to find the equation of the line that passes through the points (0, 4) and (13, 1.9).
  The slope of the line is $\frac{1.9-4}{13-0}=-\frac{21}{130}$.
  The y-intercept of the line is 4.
  Therefore, the linear function that models the production is $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130} t+4$.
  The answer is C: $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130} t+4$.
Action: Answer("C")

Thought:

  The slope $m$ of the function represents the rate of decrease in million barrels per year.

  $f(t)-4=-\frac{2.1}{13}t$
  $f(t)= -\frac{2.1}{13}t + 4$

Question: Townsend Realty purchased the Glenview Street property and received a $40 \%$ discount off the original price along with an additional $20 \%$ off the discounted price for purchasing the property in cash. Which of the following best approximates the original price, in dollars, of the Glenview Street property?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 350,000$
  B: $\$ 291,700$
  C: $\$ 233,300$
  D: $\$ 175,000$
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's assume the original price of the property is $x$ dollars.
Townsend Realty received a $40 \%$ discount off the original price, which means they paid $60 \%$ of the original price.
Therefore, the price after the first discount is $0.6x$ dollars.
They also received an additional $20 \%$ off the discounted price for purchasing the property in cash.
Therefore, the final price after both discounts is $0.8(0.6x) = 0.48x$ dollars.
We need to find the original price, which is $x$ dollars.
We can set up an equation: $0.48x = x - 0.4x$ (the final price is equal to the original price minus the $40 \%$ discount).
Simplifying the equation, we get $0.08x = x \cdot 0.4$, which means $x = \frac{0.4}{0.08}x = 5x$.
Therefore, the original price of the property is $\frac{1}{5}$ of the final price, which is $\frac{1}{5} \cdot \$ 175,000 = \$ 35,000$.
However, we need to select the answer choice that best approximates the original price.

Question: The formula below is often used by project managers to compute $E$, the estimated time to complete a job, where $O$ is the shortest completion time, $P$ is the longest completion time, and $M$ is the most likely completion time.$$E=\frac{O+4 M+P}{6}$$Which of the following correctly gives $P$ in terms of $E, O$, and $M$ ?
Choices:
  A: $P=6 E-O-4 M$
  B: $P=-6 E+O+4 M$
  C: $P=\frac{O+4 M+E}{6}$
  D: $P=\frac{O+4 M-E}{6}$

  $$E=\frac{O+4 M+P}{6}$$
  $$6E=O+4M+P$$
  $$P=6E-O-4M$$
  Therefore, the answer is A: $P=6E-O-4M$.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 49 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $f(x)$ \\\hline1 & 5 \\\hline3 & 13 \\\hline5 & 21 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of the linear function $f$ are shown in the table above. Which of the following defines $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=2 x+3$
  B: $f(x)=3 x+2$
  C: $f(x)=4 x+1$
  D: $f(x)=5 x$
Response 0:
Thought:
  If $f$ is a linear function, then its graph is a straight line.
  We can use the two points $(1,5)$ and $(3,13)$ to find the slope of the line.
  The slope of the line is $\frac{13-5}{3-1}=4$.
  Since $f(1)=5$, the $y$-intercept of the line is $(0,5-4(1))=(0,1)$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $f(x)=4x+1$.
  The answer is C: $f(x)=4 x+1$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  To determine the equation of the linear function $f$, we need to find the slope and the y-intercept.
  The slope is the change in $f(x)$ divided by the change in $x$.
  The change in $f(x)$ from 1 to 3 is $13-5=8$.
  The change in $x$ from 1 to 3 is $3-1=2$.
  Therefore, the slope is $\frac{8}{2}=4$.
  To find the y-intercept, we can use any point on the line. Let's use the point (1,5).
  The equation of the line in slope-intercept form is $f(x)=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  Plugging in the values we found, we get $f(x)=4x+1$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $f(x)=4 x+1$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  To determine the equation of a linear function, we need to find the slope and the y-intercept.
  The slope of a linear function is given by the formula: $m=\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}$, where $\Delta y$ is the change in y and $\Delta x$ is the change in x.
  We can find the slope by using any two points from the table.
  Let's use the first and second rows: $m=\frac{13-5}{3-1}=4$
  The y-intercept is the value of $f(x)$ when $x=0$.
  We can use the first row to find the y-intercept: $5=4(1)+b \Rightarrow b=1$
  Therefore, the equation of the linear function is $f(x)=4x+1$.
  The answer is C: $f(x)=4 x+1$.

  Using the points $(1,5)$ and $(3,13)$, we can find the slope of the line passing through them: $m = \frac{13 - 5}{3 - 1} = 4$.
  The y-intercept of the line can be found by substituting one of the points and the slope into the point-slope form of the equation of a line: $y - y_1 = m(x - x_1)$.
  Using the point $(1,5)$ and the slope $m = 4$, we get: $y - 5 = 4(x - 1)$, which simplifies to $y = 4x + 1$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $f(x) = 4x + 1$.

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& y<-x+a \\& y>x+b\end{aligned}$$In the $x y$-plane, if $(0,0)$ is a solution to the system of inequalities above, which of the following relationships between $a$ and $b$ must be true?
Choices:
  A: $a>b$
  B: $b>a$
  C: $|a|>|b|$
  D: $a=-b$
Response 0:
Thought:

  If $a>b$, then $|a|>|b|$ and $a$ cannot be equal to $-b$.

  If $a=-b$, then $|a|=|b|$ and $a>b$ and $b>a$ are both false.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 54 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What value of $x$ satisfies the equation $3 x+3=27$ ?
Choices:
  A: 3
  B: 8
  C: 10
  D: 27
Response 0:
Thought:
  To solve for $x$, we need to isolate $x$ on one side of the equation.
  We can start by subtracting 3 from both sides of the equation.
  $3x + 3 - 3 = 27 - 3$
  Simplifying the left side of the equation, we get:
  $3x = 24$
  To solve for $x$, we can divide both sides of the equation by 3.
  $3x/3 = 24/3$
  Simplifying the left side of the equation, we get:
  $x = 8$
  Therefore, the value of $x$ that satisfies the equation $3x + 3 = 27$ is 8.
  The answer is B: 8.

Question: Keith modeled the growth over several hundred years of a tree population by estimating the number of the trees' pollen grains per square centimeter that were deposited each year within layers of a lake's sediment. He estimated there were 310 pollen grains per square centimeter the first year the grains were deposited, with a $1 \%$ annual increase in the number of grains per square centimeter thereafter. Which of the following functions models $P(t)$, the number of pollen grains per square centimeter $t$ years after the first year the grains were deposited?
Choices:
  A: $P(t)=310^{t}$
  B: $P(t)=310^{1.01 t}$
  C: $P(t)=310(0.99)^{t}$
  D: $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The initial number of pollen grains per square centimeter is 310.
  The annual increase in the number of pollen grains per square centimeter is $1 \%$.
  The function that models the number of pollen grains per square centimeter $t$ years after the first year the grains were deposited is of the form $P(t)=310(1+r)^{t}$, where $r$ is the annual rate of increase.
  Since the annual increase is $1 \%$, we have $r=0.01$.
  Therefore, the function that models the number of pollen grains per square centimeter $t$ years after the first year the grains were deposited is $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$.
  The answer is D: $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The initial number of pollen grains per square centimeter is 310.
  The annual increase is $1 \%$.
  The function that models the growth of the pollen grains per square centimeter over time is an exponential function.
  The general form of an exponential function is $f(x)=ab^{x}$, where $a$ is the initial value and $b$ is the growth factor.
  Since the annual increase is $1 \%$, the growth factor is $1+0.01=1.01$.
  Therefore, the function that models the growth of the pollen grains per square centimeter over time is $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$.
  The answer is D: $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$.

Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|c|c|c|}\hlineList A & 1 & 2 & 3 & 4 & 5 & 6 \\\hlineList B & 2 & 3 & 3 & 4 & 4 & 5 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows two lists of numbers. Which of the following is a true statement comparing list $\mathrm{A}$ and list B ?
Choices:
  A: The means are the same, and the standard deviations are different.
  B: The means are the same, and the standard deviations are the same.
  C: The means are different, and the standard deviations are different.
  D: The means are different, and the standard deviations are the same.

  To compare the means and standard deviations of the two lists, we need to calculate them.
  The mean of list A is $\frac{1+2+3+4+5+6}{6}=3.5$.

  The standard deviation of list A is $\sqrt{\frac{(1-3.5)^2+(2-3.5)^2+(3-3.5)^2+(4-3.5)^2+(5-3.5)^2+(6-3.5)^2}{6}}\approx1.71$.

  Therefore, the means are the same, but the standard deviations are different.
  The answer is A: The means are the same, and the standard deviations are different.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 57 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$C=75 h+125$$The equation above gives the amount $C$, in dollars, an electrician charges for a job that takes $h$ hours. Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland each hired this electrician. The electrician worked 2 hours longer on Ms. Sanchez's job than on Mr. Roland's job. How much more did the electrician charge Ms. Sanchez than Mr. Roland?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 75$
  B: $\$ 125$
  C: $\$ 150$
  D: $\$ 275$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's say Mr. Roland's job took $x$ hours.
  Ms. Sanchez's job took 2 hours longer, so it took $x+2$ hours.
  We can use the equation to calculate the cost of each job.
  For Mr. Roland's job, the cost is $C=75x+125$ dollars.
  For Ms. Sanchez's job, the cost is $C=75(x+2)+125=75x+225$ dollars.
  The difference in cost is $75x+225-(75x+125)=100$ dollars.
  Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$100$ more than Mr. Roland.
  The answer is not one of the choices. 
  The closest answer is C: $\$150$, which is not the exact answer but it's the most likely answer. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's first find out how many hours the electrician worked on Mr. Roland's job.
  Let $h$ be the number of hours the electrician worked on Mr. Roland's job.
  Then, the electrician worked $(h+2)$ hours on Ms. Sanchez's job.
  The cost of Mr. Roland's job is $C=75h+125$.
  The cost of Ms. Sanchez's job is $C=75(h+2)+125$.
  We need to find the difference between the cost of Ms. Sanchez's job and Mr. Roland's job.
  Difference $=C_{Sanchez}-C_{Roland}=75(h+2)+125-(75h+125)=150$
  Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$150$ more than Mr. Roland.
  The answer is C: $\$150$.

  $C_R=75h_R+125$ (the amount Mr. Roland was charged)
  $C_S=75(h_R+2)+125=75h_R+175$ (the amount Ms. Sanchez was charged)
  The difference between the two charges is $C_S-C_R=75h_R+175-(75h_R+125)=50$.
  Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$50$ more than Mr. Roland.
  The answer is not one of the available choices, so we select the most likely answer, which is A: $\$75$.
Action: Answer("A")

Question: If the 180 food calories in a granola bar come entirely from $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate, which of the following expresses $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  C: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p-c)$
  D: $f=20+\frac{9}{4}(p+c)$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The 180 food calories in a granola bar come entirely from $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate.
  The energy per gram of protein is 4.0 food calories.
  The energy per gram of fat is 9.0 food calories.
  The energy per gram of carbohydrate is 4.0 food calories.
  Therefore, the total energy in the granola bar can be expressed as $4p+9f+4c=180$.
  We need to express $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$.
  Rearranging the equation $4p+9f+4c=180$ gives $9f=180-4p-4c$.
  Dividing both sides by 9 gives $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.

Context: $$.\begin{aligned}.& S(P)=\frac{1}{2} P+40 \\.& D(P)=220-P.\end{aligned}.$$.The quantity of a product supplied and the quantity of the product demanded in an economic market are functions of the price of the product. The functions above are the estimated supply and demand functions for a certain product. The function $S(P)$ gives the quantity of the product supplied to the market when the price is $P$ dollars, and the function $D(P)$ gives the quantity of the product demanded by the market when the price is $P$ dollars.
Question: At what price will the quantity of the product supplied to the market equal the quantity of the product demanded by the market?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 90$
  B: $\$ 120$
  C: $\$ 133$
  D: $\$ 155$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The quantity of the product supplied to the market will equal the quantity of the product demanded by the market when $S(P)=D(P)$.
  Substituting the given functions, we have $\frac{1}{2} P+40=220-P$.
  Solving for $P$, we get $P=133$.
  Therefore, the price at which the quantity of the product supplied to the market equals the quantity of the product demanded by the market is $\$ 133$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:

Substituting the given functions, we get:
$$\frac{1}{2}P+40=220-P$$
Simplifying and solving for $P$, we get:
$$\frac{3}{2}P=180$$
$$P=120$$
Therefore, the price at which the quantity of the product supplied equals the quantity of the product demanded is $\$120$.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 62 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$$In the equation above, $k$ is a constant. If $x=9$, what is the value of $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 7
  C: 16
  D: 79
Response 0:
Thought:
  $$\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$$
  We are given that $x=9$.
  Substituting $x=9$ in the equation above, we get:
  $$\sqrt{k+2}-9=0$$
  Adding 9 to both sides, we get:
  $$\sqrt{k+2}=9$$
  Squaring both sides, we get:
  $$k+2=81$$
  Subtracting 2 from both sides, we get:
  $$k=79$$
  Therefore, the value of $k$ is 79.
Action: Answer("D")

  Therefore, $k=79$.

  Squaring both sides, we get $k+2=x^2$
  Substituting $x=9$, we get $k+2=81$
  Solving for $k$, we get $k=79$
  Therefore, the answer is D: 79.
Action: Answer("D")

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 64 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$2 a x-15=3(x+5)+5(x-1)$$In the equation above, $a$ is a constant. If no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, what is the value of $a$ ?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 2
  C: 4
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought:
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  $$2ax-15=3x+15+5x-5$$
  $$2ax-15=8x+10$$
  $$2ax-8x=10+15$$
  $$x(2a-8)=25$$
  $$x=\frac{25}{2a-8}$$
  Since no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, the denominator of the expression for $x$ must be equal to zero.
  $$2a-8=0$$
  $$2a=8$$
  $$a=4$$
  Therefore, the answer is C: 4.
Action: Answer("C")

  Therefore, $a-4$ must be equal to 0.
  Thus, $a=4$.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 67 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The function $f$ is defined by $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$. The graph of $f$ in the $x y$-plane is a parabola. Which of the following intervals contains the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: $-4<x<-3$
  B: $-3<x<1$
  C: $1<x<3$
  D: $3<x<4$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The vertex of a parabola is located at the point where the $x$-coordinate is equal to $-\frac{b}{2a}$, where $a$ and $b$ are the coefficients of the quadratic function.
  The quadratic function $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$ can be expanded to $f(x)=x^2+4x+3$.
  The coefficient of $x^2$ is $a=1$ and the coefficient of $x$ is $b=4$.
  Therefore, the $x$-coordinate of the vertex is $-\frac{b}{2a}=-2$.
  The answer is the interval that contains $-2$.
  The only interval that contains $-2$ is B: $-3<x<1$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The vertex of a parabola is located at the point where the slope of the curve changes sign.
  The slope of the curve changes sign at the vertex because the curve changes from moving downwards to moving upwards or vice versa.
  The function $f$ is a quadratic function in standard form, $f(x)=ax^2+bx+c$.
  The vertex of the parabola is located at the point $(-\frac{b}{2a}, f(-\frac{b}{2a}))$.
  The function $f$ can be rewritten as $f(x)=x^2+4x+3$.
  Therefore, the vertex of the parabola is located at the point $(-2, -1)$.
  The $x$-coordinate of the vertex is $-2$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $-4<x<-3$.
Action: Answer("A")

  The vertex of this parabola is at $(-\frac{b}{2a}, f(-\frac{b}{2a}))$.
  In this case, $a=1$ and $b=4$, so the $x$-coordinate of the vertex is $-\frac{b}{2a}=-2$.
  Therefore, the answer is the interval that contains $-2$.

  B: $-\frac{4}{5}$
  C: $-\frac{2}{3}$
  D: 4

  Combining like terms gives $6x-8=9x-6$.
  Subtracting $6x$ from both sides gives $-8=3x-6$.
  Adding 6 to both sides gives $-2=3x$.
  Dividing both sides by 3 gives $-\frac{2}{3}=x$.
  Substituting $-\frac{2}{3}$ for $x$ in $3x-2$ gives $3\left(-\frac{2}{3}\right)-2=-2-2=\boxed{\textbf{(A) }-4}$.

Topic: Math
Question: $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$Clayton will mix $x$ milliliters of a $10 \%$ by mass saline solution with $y$ milliliters of a $20 \%$ by mass saline solution in order to create an $18 \%$ by mass saline solution. The equation above represents this situation. If Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution, how many milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution must he use?
Choices:
  A: 5
  B: 25
  C: 50
  D: 100
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's solve for $x$ in terms of $y$ using the given equation.
  $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$
  $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18x+0.18y$$
  $$0.02 x=0.02y$$
  $$x=y$$
  If Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution, then he will use $y=100$ milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution.
  Since $x=y$, he will use $x=100$ milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 100.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We are given that Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ saline solution.
  Let $x$ be the number of milliliters of the $10 \%$ saline solution.
  We can substitute the given values into the equation and solve for $x$.
  $$0.10 x+0.20(100)=0.18(x+100)$$
  $$0.10 x+20=0.18 x+18$$
  $$0.08 x=2$$
  $$x=25$$
  Therefore, Clayton must use 25 milliliters of the $10 \%$ saline solution.
  The answer is B: 25.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 70 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What are the solutions to $3 x^{2}+12 x+6=0 ?$
Choices:
  A: $x=-2 \pm \sqrt{2}$
  B: $x=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{30}}{3}$
  C: $x=-6 \pm \sqrt{2}$
  D: $x=-6 \pm 6 \sqrt{2}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can solve the quadratic equation by using the quadratic formula: $x=\frac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^{2}-4 a c}}{2 a}$ where $a=3, b=12,$ and $c=6$.
  Substituting the values, we get $x=\frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{12^{2}-4 \cdot 3 \cdot 6}}{2 \cdot 3}$
  Simplifying, we get $x=\frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{72}}{6}$
  Further simplifying, we get $x=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{2}}{2}$
  Therefore, the answer is A: $x=-2 \pm \sqrt{2}$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We can start by dividing both sides of the equation by 3 to simplify it.
  $3 x^{2}+12 x+6=0$ becomes $x^{2}+4 x+2=0$
  We can use the quadratic formula to solve for x: $x=\frac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^{2}-4 a c}}{2 a}$, where $a=1, b=4,$ and $c=2$.
  Substituting the values, we get $x=\frac{-4 \pm \sqrt{4^{2}-4 \cdot 1 \cdot 2}}{2 \cdot 1}$.
  Simplifying this expression, we get $x=\frac{-4 \pm \sqrt{16-8}}{2}$.
  This simplifies to $x=\frac{-4 \pm 2 \sqrt{2}}{2}$.
  We can further simplify this expression by factoring out a 2 in the numerator and canceling it with the denominator.
  This gives us $x=-2 \pm \sqrt{2}$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $x=-2 \pm \sqrt{2}$.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 9:
Thought:
  To solve the quadratic equation $3 x^{2}+12 x+6=0,$ we can use the quadratic formula $x=\frac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^{2}-4 a c}}{2 a}$ where $a=3, b=12,$ and $c=6.$
  Substituting the values of $a, b,$ and $c$ into the quadratic formula, we get $x=\frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{12^{2}-4 \cdot 3 \cdot 6}}{2 \cdot 3}.$
  Simplifying the expression inside the square root, we get $x=\frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{96}}{6}.$
  Factoring $96$ into $16 \cdot 6,$ we can simplify the expression further to get $x=\frac{-12 \pm 4 \sqrt{6}}{3}.$
  Therefore, the solutions to the equation are $x=-2 \pm \frac{2 \sqrt{6}}{3}.$
  We can simplify this expression further to get $x=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{24}}{3}.$
  Factoring $24$ into $4 \cdot 6,$ we get $x=-2 \pm \frac{2 \sqrt{6}}{3}=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{4} \sqrt{6}}{3}=-2 \pm \frac{2 \sqrt{6}}{3}.$
  Therefore, the answer is B: $x=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{30}}{3}.$

Question: Which of the following is equivalent to $2\left(x^{2}-x\right)+3\left(x^{2}-x\right) ?$
Choices:
  A: $5 x^{2}-5 x$
  B: $5 x^{2}+5 x$
  C: $5 x$
  D: $5 x^{2}$

  $$
  2\left(x^{2}-x\right)+3\left(x^{2}-x\right) = (2+3)(x^{2}-x) = 5(x^{2}-x)
  $$
  Therefore, the expression is equivalent to $5(x^{2}-x)$.
  The answer is D: $5 x^{2}-5 x$.

$= 5x^2 - x$

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 75 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In planning maintenance for a city's infrastructure, a civil engineer estimates that, starting from the present, the population of the city will decrease by 10 percent every 20 years. If the present population of the city is 50,000, which of the following expressions represents the engineer's estimate of the population of the city $t$ years from now?
Choices:
  A: $50,000(0.1)^{20 t}$
  B: $50,000(0.1)^{\frac{t}{20}}$
  C: $50,000(0.9)^{20 t}$
  D: $50,000(0.9)^{\frac{t}{20}}$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The population of the city will decrease by 10% every 20 years.
  This means that the population will be multiplied by 0.9 every 20 years.
  The present population of the city is 50,000.
  We need to find an expression that represents the population of the city t years from now.
  If t is a multiple of 20, then the population will be multiplied by (0.9)^(t/20).
  If t is not a multiple of 20, then we can express t as 20n + r, where n is a non-negative integer and r is the remainder when t is divided by 20.
  The population of the city t years from now can be expressed as 50,000(0.9)^(20n+r).
  This can be simplified as 50,000(0.9)^(20n)(0.9)^r.
  Since (0.9)^20n is a constant, we can write the expression as 50,000(0.9)^20n(0.9)^r.
  This can be further simplified as 50,000(0.9)^r(0.9)^20n.
  Therefore, the expression that represents the population of the city t years from now is 50,000(0.9)^(t/20) or 50,000(0.9)^{(t-20n)}.
  The answer is B: $50,000(0.1)^{\frac{t}{20}}$.
Action: Answer("B")

Question: A rectangle was altered by increasing its length by 10 percent and decreasing its width by $p$ percent. If these alterations decreased the area of the rectangle by 12 percent, what is the value of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: 12
  B: 15
  C: 20
  D: 22
Response 0:
Thought:
Let the original length and width of the rectangle be $l$ and $w$, respectively.
The original area of the rectangle is $lw$.
After the alterations, the new length and width of the rectangle are $1.1l$ and $(1-\frac{p}{100})w$, respectively.
The new area of the rectangle is $(1.1l)(1-\frac{p}{100})w$.
We are given that the new area is 12 percent less than the original area, so we have the equation:
$$
(1.1l)(1-\frac{p}{100})w = 0.88lw
$$
Simplifying this equation, we get:
$$
1.1(1-\frac{p}{100}) = 0.88
$$
Solving for $p$, we get:
$$
p = \frac{22}{3}
$$
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:

  The original area of the rectangle is L x W.

  The new area of the rectangle is (1.1L) x (1-p/100)W.

  (1.1L) x (1-p/100)W = 0.88LW
  Simplifying this equation, we get:
  1.1(1-p/100) = 0.88
  Solving for p, we get:
  p = 20
  Therefore, the value of p is 20.

  The new area of the rectangle is (1.1L)*(1-p/100)W = 0.88(L*W).
  We know that the new area is 0.88 times the original area.
  Therefore, we can set up the equation 0.88(L*W) = L*W - 0.12(L*W) and solve for p.
  Simplifying the equation, we get 0.12(L*W) = 0.1L*W + p/100*W*L.
  Dividing both sides by L*W, we get 0.12 = 0.1 + p/100*(1-p/100).
  Multiplying both sides by 100, we get 12 = 10 + p*(100-p)/10000.
  Rearranging the terms, we get p^2 - 100p + 200 = 0.
  Using the quadratic formula, we get p = (100 +/- sqrt(100^2 - 4*1*200))/2.
  The positive solution is p = (100 + sqrt(10000 - 800))/2 = (100 + 20)/2 = 60.
  Therefore, the value of p is 60.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 79 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $(a x+2)(b x+7)=15 x^{2}+c x+14$ for all values of $x$, and $a+b=8$, what are the two possible values for $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: 3 and 5
  B: 6 and 35
  C: 10 and 21
  D: 31 and 41
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can expand the left side of the equation and compare the coefficients of the resulting quadratic equation with the given quadratic equation to find the value of c.
  Expanding the left side of the equation gives us:
  $a b x^{2}+(7 a+2 b) x+14=15 x^{2}+c x+14$
  Comparing the coefficients of the quadratic equation gives us:
  $ab=15$
  $7a+2b=c$
  We know that $a+b=8$, so we can solve for $a$ and $b$:
  $a=8-b$
  Substituting into the first equation gives us:
  $(8-b) b=15$
  $b^{2}-8 b+15=0$
  $(b-5)(b-3)=0$
  Therefore, $b=5$ or $b=3$.
  Substituting these values into $7a+2b=c$ gives us:
  $b=5$: $7a+10=c$, $a=1$, $c=17$
  $b=3$: $7a+6=c$, $a=1$, $c=13$
  Therefore, the two possible values for $c$ are 13 and 17.

  Multiplying both sides by $a$, we get:

$7a^2 + 30 = ac$

  We can substitute the value of $ab$ from the first equation to get:

$7a^2 + 30 = 15a$

$7a^2 - 15a + 30 = 0$

  We can use the quadratic formula to solve for $a$:

$a = \frac{15 \pm \sqrt{15^2 - 4(7)(30)}}{2(7)}$

$a = \frac{15 \pm \sqrt{225 - 840}}{14}$

$a = \frac{15 \pm \sqrt{-615}}{14}$

  Since the discriminant is negative, there are no real solutions for $a$. Therefore, there are no real solutions for $c$.

  The answer is None of the Above.

  Therefore, the two possible values for $c$ are 37 and 70.

Question: What is the set of all solutions to the equation $\sqrt{x+2}=-x ?$
Choices:
  A: $\{-1,2\}$
  B: $\{-1\}$
  C: $\{2\}$
  D: There are no solutions to the given equation.
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can square both sides of the equation $\sqrt{x+2}=-x$ to get rid of the square root.
  Squaring both sides gives $x+2=x^2$.
  Rearranging this equation gives $x^2-x-2=0$.
  Factoring this quadratic equation gives $(x-2)(x+1)=0$.
  Therefore, the solutions to the equation are $x=2$ and $x=-1$.
  The answer is A: $\{-1,2\}$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Since the square root of a number is always non-negative, $x+2$ must be non-negative.
  Therefore, $x \geq -2$.
  Squaring both sides of the equation $\sqrt{x+2}=-x$, we get $x+2=x^2$.
  Rearranging, we get $x^2-x-2=0$.
  Factoring the quadratic equation, we get $(x-2)(x+1)=0$.
  Therefore, $x=2$ or $x=-1$.
  However, $x=-1$ does not satisfy the condition $x \geq -2$.
  Therefore, the only solution is $x=2$.
  The answer is C: $\{2\}$.

  -2 is equal to -2, so it is a solution.

The table shows the amount, in dollars, the company paid for each property and the corresponding monthly rental price, in dollars, the company charges for the property at each of the five locations. 23The relationship between the monthly rental price $r$, in dollars, and the property's purchase price $p$, in thousands of dollars, can be represented by a linear function. Which of the following functions represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $r(p)=2.5 p-870$
  B: $r(p)=5 p+165$
  C: $r(p)=6.5 p+440$
  D: $r(p)=7.5 p-10$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to find a linear function that represents the relationship between the monthly rental price and the property's purchase price.
  We can use the formula for the equation of a line: $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  We can use two points from the table to find the slope of the line.
  We can use the point-slope form of a line to find the equation of the line.
  We need to convert the purchase price from dollars to thousands of dollars.
  
Action: 
  We can use the points $(128, 950)$ and $(450, 3365)$ to find the slope of the line.
  The slope is $\frac{3365-950}{450-128}=\frac{2415}{322}=7.5$.
  The y-intercept is the monthly rental price when the purchase price is 0, which doesn't make sense in this context.
  We can use the point-slope form of the line with the point $(128, 950)$ and the slope $7.5$ to find the equation of the line.
  The equation is $r(p)-950=7.5(p-128)$.
  Simplifying, we get $r(p)=7.5p-10$.
  Therefore, the answer is D: $r(p)=7.5 p-10$.

  C: 700 meters

  If Nate walks 25 meters in 13.7 seconds, then he walks x meters in 240 seconds, where x is the distance we want to find.
  The proportion is 25/13.7 = x/240.
  Solving for x, we get x = 25/13.7 x 240 = 438.96 meters.

Question: Roberto is an insurance agent who sells two types of policies: a $\$ 50,000$ policy and a $\$ 100,000$ policy. Last month, his goal was to sell at least 57 insurance policies. While he did not meet his goal, the total value of the policies he sold was over $\$ 3,000,000$. Which of the following systems of inequalities describes $x$, the possible number of $\$ 50,000$ policies, and $y$, the possible number of $\$ 100,000$ policies, that Roberto sold last month?
Choices:
  A: $x+y<57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y<3,000,000$
  B: $x+y>57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y>3,000,000$
  C: $x+y<57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y>3,000,000$
  D: $x+y>57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y<3,000,000$
Response 0:
Thought:

  We know that $x+y<57$ because Roberto did not meet his goal of selling at least 57 policies.
  We also know that $50,000x+100,000y>3,000,000$ because the total value of the policies sold was over $\$ 3,000,000$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $x+y<57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y<3,000,000$.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 87 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& b=2.35+0.25 x \\& c=1.75+0.40 x\end{aligned}$$In the equations above, $b$ and $c$ represent the price per pound, in dollars, of beef and chicken, respectively, $x$ weeks after July 1 during last summer. What was the price per pound of beef when it was equal to the price per pound of chicken?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 2.60$
  B: $\$ 2.85$
  C: $\$ 2.95$
  D: $\$ 3.35$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to find the value of $x$ when $b=c$.
  Substitute the given expressions for $b$ and $c$ and solve for $x$.
  Then, substitute the value of $x$ into either equation to find the price per pound of beef.
  The answer is the price per pound of beef when it was equal to the price per pound of chicken.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We need to find the value of $x$ when $b=c$.
  We can set the two equations equal to each other and solve for $x$.
  $$2.35+0.25x=1.75+0.40x$$
  $$0.15x=0.60$$
  $$x=4$$
  We can substitute $x=4$ into either equation to find the price per pound.
  $$b=2.35+0.25(4)=\boxed{\$ 2.45}$$
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 2:
Thought:
  We need to find the value of $x$ when $b=c$.
  Substitute $b$ and $c$ in terms of $x$.
  Solve for $x$.
  Substitute the value of $x$ in $b$ to find the price per pound of beef.
Action: Answer("C") $\$ 2.95$

Solution:
  Set $b=c$.
  $$2.35+0.25x=1.75+0.40x$$
  Solve for $x$.
  \begin{align*}
  0.15x&=0.60 \\
  x&=4
  \end{align*}

Question: The first year Eleanor organized a fund-raising event, she invited 30 people. For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year. If $f(n)$ is the number of people invited to the fund-raiser $n$ years after Eleanor began organizing the event, which of the following statements best describes the function $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: The function $f$ is a decreasing linear function.
  B: The function $f$ is an increasing linear function.
  C: The function $f$ is a decreasing exponential function.
  D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
Response 0:
Thought:
  In the first year, Eleanor invited 30 people.
  For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year.
  This means that in the second year, she invited 60 people, in the third year, she invited 120 people, and so on.
  We can write this as $f(1) = 30$, $f(2) = 60$, $f(3) = 120$, and so on.
  The function $f$ is increasing because each term is greater than the previous term.
  The function $f$ is not linear because the difference between consecutive terms is not constant.
  The function $f$ is exponential because each term is obtained by multiplying the previous term by a constant factor (in this case, 2).
  Therefore, the answer is D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  In the first year, Eleanor invited 30 people.
  For the second year, she invited double the number of people she had invited in the previous year, which is $2 \times 30 = 60$ people.
  For the third year, she invited double the number of people she had invited in the previous year, which is $2 \times 60 = 120$ people.
  For the fourth year, she invited double the number of people she had invited in the previous year, which is $2 \times 120 = 240$ people.
  For the fifth year, she invited double the number of people she had invited in the previous year, which is $2 \times 240 = 480$ people.
  We can see that the number of people invited is increasing exponentially.
  Therefore, the function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
  The answer is D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.

Question: Survey Results\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|}\hlineAnswer & Percent \\\hlineNever & $31.3 \%$ \\\hlineRarely & $24.3 \%$ \\\hlineOften & $13.5 \%$ \\\hlineAlways & $30.9 \%$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows the results of a survey in which tablet users were asked how often they would watch video advertisements in order to access streaming content for free. Based on the table, which of the following is closest to the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never"?
Choices:
  A: 0.31
  B: 0.38
  C: 0.45
  D: 0.69
Response 0:
Thought: 
  We want to find the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never".
  Let's call this probability P(Always|Not Never).
  We can use Bayes' Theorem to find P(Always|Not Never).
  P(Always|Not Never) = P(Not Never|Always) * P(Always) / P(Not Never)
  We know that P(Always) = 30.9% and P(Not Never) = 100% - P(Never) = 68.7%.
  To find P(Not Never|Always), we need to look at the table and find the percentage of people who answered "Not Never" among those who answered "Always". This is 100% - 0% = 100%.
  Plugging in the values, we get:
  P(Always|Not Never) = 100% * 30.9% / 68.7% = 0.45 (rounded to two decimal places).
  Therefore, the closest answer is C: 0.45.

  A: $640 x+880 y \geq 9,700$ $x+y \leq 10$ $x \geq 3$ $y \geq 1$

  C: $640 x+880 y \geq 9,700$ $x+y \geq 10$ $x \leq 3$ $y \leq 1$

  The budget for paying the staff members is no more than $\$ 9,700$ per week.
  The cost of hiring $x$ junior directors is $640x$ per week.
  The cost of hiring $y$ senior directors is $880y$ per week.
  Therefore, the system of inequalities that represents the conditions described is:
  $640x+880y \leq 9700$ (budget constraint)
  $x+y \geq 10$ (at least 10 staff members)
  $x \geq 3$ (at least 3 junior directors)
  $y \geq 1$ (at least 1 senior director)
  The answer is A: $640 x+880 y \geq 9,700$ $x+y \leq 10$ $x \geq 3$ $y \geq 1$.

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& 2 x-3 y=-14 \\& 3 x-2 y=-6\end{aligned}$$If $(x, y)$ is a solution to the system of equations above, what is the value of $x-y$ ?
Choices:
  A: -20
  B: $\quad-8$
  C: -4
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can solve the system of equations by using elimination method.
  Multiplying the first equation by 2 and the second equation by 3, we get:
  $$\begin{aligned}& 4 x-6 y=-28 \\& 9 x-6 y=-18\end{aligned}$$
  Subtracting the second equation from the first, we get:
  $$-5x = -10$$
  Solving for x, we get:
  $$x = 2$$
  Substituting x = 2 into the first equation, we get:
  $$2(2) - 3y = -14$$
  Solving for y, we get:
  $$y = 8$$
  Therefore, $(x,y) = (2,8)$ and $x-y = -6$.
  The answer is B: -8.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 92 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A line in the $x y$-plane passes through the origin and has a slope of $\frac{1}{7}$. Which of the following points lies on the line?
Choices:
  A: $(0,7)$
  B: $(1,7)$
  C: $(7,7)$
  D: $(14,2)$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The equation of a line in point-slope form is $y-y_1=m(x-x_1)$, where $m$ is the slope and $(x_1,y_1)$ is a point on the line.
  Since the line passes through the origin, we have $y-0=\frac{1}{7}(x-0)$, which simplifies to $y=\frac{1}{7}x$.
  We can substitute the coordinates of each point into this equation to see which point lies on the line.
  A: $(0,7)$ does not lie on the line since $y\neq\frac{1}{7}x$.
  B: $(1,7)$ does not lie on the line since $y\neq\frac{1}{7}x$.
  C: $(7,7)$ does lie on the line since $y=\frac{1}{7}(7)=1$ and $x=7$.
  D: $(14,2)$ does not lie on the line since $y\neq\frac{1}{7}x$.
  Therefore, the point that lies on the line is C: $(7,7)$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The equation of a line in slope-intercept form is $y = mx + b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  Since the line passes through the origin, the y-intercept is 0.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $y = \frac{1}{7}x$.
  To check which point lies on the line, we substitute the coordinates of each point into the equation of the line and see if the equation is true.
  For point A, $y = \frac{1}{7}(0) = 0$, which is not equal to 7. Therefore, point A does not lie on the line.
  For point B, $y = \frac{1}{7}(1) = \frac{1}{7}$, which is not equal to 7. Therefore, point B does not lie on the line.
  For point C, $y = \frac{1}{7}(7) = 1$, which is equal to 7. Therefore, point C lies on the line.
  For point D, $y = \frac{1}{7}(14) = 2$, which is not equal to 2. Therefore, point D does not lie on the line.
  Therefore, the point that lies on the line is C.
